Intention for Tayammum: Restricted Acts and the Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on restricted intention for tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid restricted intentions for tayammum and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding tayammum for embracing Islam.

Core Idea
Tayammum's restricted intention must target an act requiring purification; otherwise, subsequent prayer is invalid.

Tayammum, like ablution, removes hadath. However, when the intention is restricted to a specific purpose, that purpose must be a worship that requires purification. This lesson unpacks the third condition for valid tayammum and examines a key intra-Hanafi difference: whether tayammum for embracing Islam makes subsequent prayer valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling on absolute intention
Start by recalling that tayammum with absolute intention (niyyah mutlaqah) or intention to remove hadath is valid for prayer. This is the baseline established in the text.
Absolute intention means intending purification without specifying an act.
2
Analyze the condition for restricted intention
When the intention is restricted (muqayyadah), it must be for an 'ibadah maqsudah – a worship that is intended in itself and requires purification. List examples given: prayer, funeral prayer, prostration of recitation, reciting Quran by a junub.
Acts like touching the Mushaf or entering a mosque do not qualify because they are not worship requiring purification.
3
Examine invalid restricted intentions
Identify cases where tayammum does not validate prayer: intending for reciting Quran while in minor impurity (since minor impurity does not forbid recitation), or for other acts like teaching, visiting graves, etc.
The key principle: if the intended act is permissible without purification, tayammum for it cannot remove hadath for prayer.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on embracing Islam
Abu Yusuf holds that tayammum for embracing Islam is valid for prayer because embracing Islam is the greatest worship. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad disagree, arguing that embracing Islam does not require prior purification. The majority considers Abu Hanifa's view most correct.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is whether someone who embraces Islam via tayammum can pray without renewing tayammum.
5
Apply the condition to new scenarios
Use the principle to evaluate other acts: e.g., tayammum for prostration of thankfulness is disputed; tayammum for touching the Mushaf is invalid for prayer.
The narration from al-Nawadir allowing tayammum with mere intention is not the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحدث لأن التيمم رافع له كالوضوء وأما إذا قيد النية بشيء فلا بد أن يكون خاصاً بينه في الشرط الثالث بقوله (أو) نية عبادة مقصودة) وهي التي لا تجب في ضمن شيء آخر بطريق التبعية فتكون قد شرعت ابتداء تقربًا إلى الله تعالى وتكون أيضاً (لا تصح بدون طهارة) فيكون المنوي إما صلاة أو جزاً للصلاة في حد ذاته كقوله نويت التيمم للصلاة، أو لصلاة الجنازة أو سجدة التلاوة، أو لقراءة القرآن، وهو جنب أو نوته لقراءة القرآن بعد انقطاع حيضها، أو نفاسها لأن كلا منها لا بد له من الطهارة وهو عبادة فلا يصلي به) أي المتيمم (إذا نوى التيمم فقط أي مجرداً من غير ملاحظة شيء مما تقدم (أو نواه) أي التيمم القراءة القرآن و) هو محدث حدثاً أصغر ولم يكن جنباً) وكذا المرأة إذا نوته للقراءة ولم تكن مخاطبة بالتطهر من حيض ونفاس الجواز قراءة المحدث لا الجنب فلو تيمم الجنب لمس بنية الإستباحة يعني أنه لما نوى إستباحة الصلاة وهي لا تكون إلا برفع الحدث فكأنه نوى رفعه أي، وهي تصح بنية رفعه وإذا حققنا النظر وجدنا كلتا النيتين السابقتين ترجع إلى نية رفع الحدث لأن نية الطهارة ترجع إلى نية الإباحة وهي ترجع إلى نية الرفع، فليتأمل. قوله: (فتصح بإطلاق النية تفريع على قوله أما نية الطهارة وليس المراد بإطلاق النية نية التيمم، فإن المصنف نص بعد على أنها لا تصح بنيته. قوله : ( وبنية رفع الحدث) تفريع على قوله : لأنّ إباحتها برفع الحدث ولا بد من ضميمة قولنا وهي تصح بنيته قوله: (وأما إذا قيد النية بشيء) عطف على مقدّر تقديره هذا إذا أطلق في النية، وينتظم صورتين صورة نية الطهارة، أو صورة نية إستباحة الصلاة وصورة نية رفع الحدث قوله : (بينه في الشرط الثالث) الأولى بينه الأمر الثالث لأن الشرط هو أحد الثلاثة المذكورة، فتأمل قوله : (وهي التي لا تجب الخ) كالصلاة بخلاف المس، فإنه وجب له بطريق التبع للتلاوة وهو في حد ذاته ليس عبادة، ولا يتقرب به إبتداء. قوله : لا تصح بدون طهارة أي أو لا تحل ليشمل قراءة القرآن لنحو الجنب . قوله : (في حد ذاته أي بالنظر إلى ذاته، والمراد أنه جزء في الجملة وإن كان يتحقق غير جزء لسبب آخر كالسجود. قوله: (كقوله نويت التيمم للصلاة) لا يظهر، بل المناسب لقوله : فيكون المنوي إما صلاة أن يكون المنوي عند التيمم الصلاة، ونحوها، أو يكون المعنى على إستباحة هذه العبادة، فيرجع إلى ما قبله. قوله : (أو لصلاة الجنازة) لو أدخلها في عموم الصلاة، فيقول : فيكون المنوي إما صلاة، ولو صلاة جنازة لكان أولى لأنها صلاة من وجه. قوله : (أو سجدة (التلاوة هذا وما بعده مثال الجزء الصلاة في الجملة. قوله: (وهو عبادة) أي مقصودة لا تصح بدون طهارة قوله فلا يصلي به تفريع على إشتراط أحد هذه الأشياء الثلاثة . قوله : ( ولم يكن جنباً) تصريح باللازم قوله : ( ولم تكن مخاطبة بالتطهر) أي بأن تكون محدثة حدثاً أصغر فقط. قوله : (لجواز قراءة المحدث) أي فهي عبادة مقصودة لكنها تحل بدون الطهارة فقد فقد الشرط الثالث قوله : (لا) الجنب أي وما في معناه. قوله: (فلو تيمم الجنب لمس المصحف، أو دخول المسجد أو تعليم الغير لا تجوز به صلاته في الأصح وكذا لزيارة القبور والآذان والإقامة والسلام ورده أو للإسلام عند عامة المشايخ وقال أبو يوسف : تصح صلاته به لدخوله في الإسلام لأنه رأس القرب، وقال أبو حنيفة ومحمد : لا تصح وهو الأصح ولو تيمم لسجدة الشكر فهو على الخلاف كما سنذكره، وفي رواية النوادر والحسن جوازه بمجرد نيته
The hadath because tayammum removes it like ablution. And as for when the intention is restricted to something, then it must be specific; he explained it in the third condition by saying (or) intention of a worship that is intended, which is not obligatory within something else by way of following, so it is legislated initially to draw near to Allah, and also it is not valid without purification. So what is intended is either prayer or a part of prayer in itself, like saying: I intend tayammum for prayer, or for funeral prayer, or prostration of recitation, or for reciting Quran while in major impurity, or she intends it for reciting Quran after the cessation of menstruation or post-partum bleeding, because each of these requires purification and is a worship. So the one performing tayammum should not pray if he intended only tayammum, i.e., mere intention without regard to anything mentioned before, or he intended it for reciting Quran while in minor impurity and not in major impurity, and similarly a woman if she intends it for recitation and she is not addressed with purification from menstruation and post-partum bleeding, because it is permissible for one in minor impurity to recite, but not for the one in major impurity. So if a person in major impurity performs tayammum for touching [the Quran] with the intention of permissibility, meaning that when he intended permissibility of prayer, which is only by removal of hadath, it is as if he intended its removal, and it is valid with the intention of its removal. And if we investigate, we find that both of the previous intentions go back to the intention of removing hadath, because the intention of purification goes back to the intention of permission, which goes back to the intention of removal. So reflect. His saying: (it is valid with absolute intention) is a branch on his saying: as for the intention of purification, and the meaning of absolute intention is not the intention of tayammum, because the author later stated that it is not valid with its intention. His saying: (and with the intention of removing hadath) is a branch on his saying: because its permissibility is by removing hadath, and it is necessary to add our saying: it is valid with its intention. His saying: (and as for when intention is restricted to something) is connected to an implied [phrase] which is: this is when the intention is absolute, and it includes two forms: the form of intention of purification, or the form of intention of permission of prayer, and the form of intention of removing hadath. His saying: (he explained it in the third condition) — it would be better to say the third matter because the condition is one of the three mentioned, so reflect. His saying: (and it is that which is not obligatory etc.) like prayer, as opposed to touching, for it becomes obligatory by way of following the recitation, and it is not in itself a worship, and one does not draw near by it initially. His saying: (it is not valid without purification) i.e., or it is not permissible, to include reciting Quran for the one in major impurity. His saying: (in itself) i.e., with regard to its essence, and the meaning is that it is a part in total, even if it is realized as not a part due to another cause like prostration. His saying: (like his saying: I intend tayammum for prayer) — it is not apparent, but the appropriate thing for his saying: so what is intended is either prayer — is that what is intended at tayammum is prayer and the like, or the meaning is for the permission of this worship, so it goes back to what is before. His saying: (or for funeral prayer) — if he included it in the generality of prayer, he would say: so what is intended is either prayer, even if funeral prayer, it would be better because it is prayer from one aspect. His saying: (or prostration of recitation) — this and what follows are examples of a part of prayer in total. His saying: (and it is a worship) i.e., intended, not valid without purification. His saying: (so he should not pray with it) is a branch on the condition of one of these three things. His saying: (and he was not in major impurity) is an explicit statement of what is necessary. His saying: (and she was not addressed with purification) i.e., that she is only in minor impurity. His saying: (because of the permissibility of the one in minor impurity to recite) i.e., it is an intended worship but it is permissible without purification, so the third condition is lost. His saying: (not) the one in major impurity i.e., and what is in its meaning. His saying: (so if a person in major impurity performs tayammum for touching the Mushaf, or entering the mosque, or teaching others, his prayer is not valid with it according to the most correct [view], and likewise for visiting graves, the call to prayer, the iqama, greeting and responding to it, or for embracing Islam according to the general mashayikh. And Abu Yusuf said: his prayer is valid with it because of his entering into Islam, for it is the chief of acts of worship. And Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said: it is not valid, and that is the most correct. And if he performs tayammum for the prostration of thankfulness, it is subject to the difference [of opinion] as we will mention. And in the narration of al-Nawadir and al-Hasan, its permissibility is by his mere intention.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of tayammum when the intention is restricted to specific acts. The text clarifies the third condition for valid tayammum: the intended act must be a worship that requires purification. The author discusses various scenarios: if one intends tayammum for prayer, funeral prayer, prostration of recitation, or reciting Quran while in major impurity, these are valid because the acts require purification. However, if one intends tayammum for reciting Quran while in minor impurity only, it is invalid because minor impurity does not prevent recitation. The passage then addresses the case of a person in major impurity performing tayammum for acts like touching the Mushaf, entering a mosque, or teaching others. According to the majority of mashayikh, such tayammum does not validate subsequent prayer because the intended act is either not a worship or does not require purification. Abu Yusuf differs for the case of embracing Islam, considering it the chief act of worship. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad maintain the majority view, and this is considered the most correct. The text also notes a narration from al-Nawadir and al-Hasan allowing tayammum with mere intention for prostration of thankfulness, but this is not relied upon.

Key Terms
نية مطلقة (niyyah mutlaqah): Absolute intention without specifying a particular act; here it refers to intending purification or permissibility of prayer without restriction.
نية مقيدة (niyyah muqayyadah): Restricted intention where the person specifies a particular act for which tayammum is performed.
عبادة مقصودة ('ibadah maqsudah): A worship that is intended in itself, not as a means to another act, and which requires purification.
إباحة الصلاة (ibahah al-salah): Permissibility of prayer, which is achieved by removal of hadath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person in major impurity performs tayammum with the intention to teach Quran to others. According to the most correct Hanafi view, is his subsequent prayer valid?
A) Yes, because teaching is a form of worship.
B) Yes, because tayammum removes major impurity.
C) No, because teaching is not a worship that requires purification.
D) No, because the intention must specify prayer.

Key Takeaway
For tayammum to permit prayer, a restricted intention must be for a worship that itself requires purification; otherwise, the tayammum does not remove hadath for prayer.

Distance from Water as a Valid Excuse for Tayammum
Defines the second condition for tayammum: the excuse of being a mile away from water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the distance that permits tayammum according to the Hanafi school and explain why predominant conjecture suffices.

Core Idea
A mile's distance from water permits tayammum – the measure is based on predominant conjecture, not exact measurement.

This passage clarifies the second condition for tayammum: the presence of a valid excuse. One primary excuse is being a mile away from pure water. The Hanafi school has established this distance based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj). The text provides detailed measurements to define a mile, but the operative ruling is that predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann) satisfies the condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
What is the second condition for tayammum validity according to the passage? It is the presence of an excuse that permits tayammum. One type of excuse is being a distance from water.
The condition is not the distance itself, but the excuse. Distance is one form of excuse.
2
Determine the required distance
What is the specific distance that makes tayammum permissible? The text states 'a mile' (mil), which is one-third of a parasang, estimated as 4000 steps or 1.5 common cubits.
The chosen (mukhtar) view is one mile, and it is the well-known (mashhur) position.
3
Understand the rationale
Why was one mile chosen? Tayammum was legislated to remove hardship (haraj). Walking that distance to fetch water would cause hardship, so tayammum is allowed.
The principle: 'ما شرع التيمم إلا لدفع الحرج' (Tayammum was only legislated to remove hardship).
4
Recognize the evidentiary standard
What level of certainty is required about the distance? The text says 'bi-ghalabati al-zann' (by predominant conjecture). This has the ruling of certainty in fiqh matters.
The jurists do not require exact measurement; reasonable estimation suffices.
5
Note the scope of application
Does this condition apply only outside inhabited areas? No, the text says 'even if his distance from it is within the city' – the excuse applies regardless of location as long as water is not available at that distance.
The water must be pure (tahur) and apparent (i.e., known to exist at that distance).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(الثاني) من شروط صحة التيمم العذر المبيح للتيمم) وهو على أنواع (كبعده) أي الشخص (ميلاً) وهو ثلث فرسخ بغلبة الظن هو المختار للحرج بالذهاب هذه المسافة وما شرع التيمم إلا لدفع الحرج وثلث الفرسخ أربعة آلاف خطوة، وهي ذراع ونصف بذراع العامة فيتيمم لبعده ميلاً ( عن ماء) ظهور (ولو) كان بعده عنه (في المصر) قوله : (كبعده أي الشخص ميلا ضبط بعضهم الميل والفرسخ، والبريد في قوله : إن الـبـــريـــد مـن الــفــراســخ أربع ولفرسخ فثلاث أميال ضــعــوا والميل ألف أي من الباعات قل والباع أربع أذرع فــتــتــبــعــوا ثم الذراع من الأصابع أربع من بعدها العشرون، ثم الإصبع شعيرات فظهر شعيرة منها إلى بطن لأخـرى تــوضــع ثم الشعيرة ست شعرات فقط من ذيل بغل ليس عن ذا مرجع قاله في الفتح والميل في اللغة منتهى مد البصر . قوله : (بغلبة الظن فإن لها حكم اليقين في الفقهيات قوله هو المختار) أي التقدير بالميل هو المختار، وهو المشهور عند الجمهور. قوله: (وهي ذراع ونصف) فجملة ذرعانه ستة آلاف، وبعضهم ضبطه في القدم بنصف ساعة . قوله : (عن ماء طهور) أي كاف.
(The second) of the conditions for the validity of tayammum is the excuse that permits tayammum, and it is of types, such as (his distance) i.e., the person (a mile), which is one-third of a parasang, based on predominant conjecture, and this is the chosen [view] due to hardship in going that distance, and tayammum was only legislated to remove hardship. One-third of a parasang is four thousand steps, and that is one and a half cubits by the common cubit. So he performs tayammum for his being a mile away (from water) that is apparent, even if his distance from it is (within the city). His saying: (like his distance i.e., the person a mile) — some have defined the mile, the parasang, and the barid in his saying: Indeed the barid is from the parasangs four, and for the parasang three miles they placed, and the mile is a thousand [cubits] of bā'āt, they said, and the bā' is four cubits, so follow, then the cubit is from the fingers four, after it twenty, then the finger is [made of] barleycorns, so a barleycorn appears from one to the belly of another placed, then the barleycorn is six hairs only from the tail of a mule, not from this reference — said in al-Fath. And the mile in language is the extent of eyesight. His saying: (by predominant conjecture, for it has the ruling of certainty in juristic matters) — his saying: (it is the chosen) i.e., the estimation by the mile is the chosen, and it is well-known among the majority. His saying: (and it is one and a half cubits) — so the total of its cubits is six thousand, and some defined it in feet as half an hour. His saying: (from pure water) i.e., sufficient.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage states the second condition for the validity of tayammum: the presence of an excuse that permits tayammum, one type being the distance from water. The relied-upon view is that a distance of one mile (approximately one-third of a parasang) is sufficient to allow tayammum. This is based on the principle of removing hardship, as tayammum was legislated for that purpose. The text provides detailed measurements: a parasang is three miles, a mile is one thousand bā'āt (a bā' is a fathom of four cubits), and a cubit is twenty-four finger-widths, each finger being six barleycorns, etc. However, for juristic purposes, the mile is defined as the distance at which water is not available and traveling to it would cause hardship. The condition also requires that the water be pure and apparent; even if the person is within a city but far from water, tayammum is permissible. The predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann) about the distance is sufficient, and it has the force of certainty in fiqh matters.

Key Terms
ميل (mil): A unit of distance equivalent to one-third of a parasang; defined by jurists as approximately 4000 steps or 1.5 common cubits.
فرسخ (farsakh): A unit of distance equal to three miles.
بغلبة الظن (bi-ghalabati al-zann): Based on predominant conjecture; sufficient for legal determination in juristic matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum distance from water that permits tayammum according to the chosen view in the Hanafi school?
A) One parasang
B) One mile
C) Two miles
D) Half a mile

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is permissible when water is a mile away, based on predominant conjecture, to remove hardship.

Tayammum for Non-Essential Acts and Validity of Salah
Ruling on valid/invalid salah after tayammum for non-prayer purposes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of salah performed with tayammum done for non-essential purposes, distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and apply the relied-upon opinion.

Core Idea
Tayammum must be intended for a purpose requiring taharah; otherwise, prayer with it is invalid.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: if a person performs tayammum for an act that does not require purification for salah—such as touching the mus-haf, entering the mosque, teaching, visiting graves, adhan, iqamah, greeting, or embracing Islam—and then prays, is that prayer valid? The majority of the Hanafi school, including Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, rule it invalid, while Abu Yusuf considers it valid. Understanding this dispute clarifies the conditions for tayammum as a substitute for wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage lists several acts for which tayammum is performed (touching mus-haf, entering mosque, etc.). The question is whether salah performed with that tayammum is valid. First, note the act: tayammum performed for a non-essential purpose.
2
State the Hanafi position and opponent
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the salah is invalid; Abu Yusuf says it is valid. The relied-upon opinion is that of the majority (invalid). Identify that this is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the opposing proof (Abu Yusuf)
Abu Yusuf argues that tayammum enters one into Islam, which is the highest act of worship, so it should suffice for any purpose. His dalil is that tayammum is a means to the greatest good.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and dalil
The majority responds that tayammum is a substitute for wudu; if the purpose does not require wudu, the tayammum does not serve as a valid substitute for prayer. They cite the hadith 'al-turab tuhur al-muslim' (earth is a purifier for the Muslim), meaning it is only a purifier for acts that require purification.
The hadith is used to show that tayammum is only valid when the act requires purification.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence: if one prays with such tayammum, according to the majority the prayer is invalid and must be repeated; according to Abu Yusuf it is valid. The text states 'wa huwa al-ashah' (it is the most correct), so the mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المصحف، أو دخول المسجد أو تعليم الغير لا تجوز به صلاته في الأصح وكذا لزيارة القبور والآذان والإقامة والسلام ورده أو للإسلام عند عامة المشايخ وقال أبو يوسف : تصح صلاته به لدخوله في الإسلام لأنه رأس القرب، وقال أبو حنيفة ومحمد : لا تصح وهو الأصح ولو تيمم لسجدة الشكر فهو على الخلاف كما سنذكره، وفي رواية النوادر والحسن جوازه بمجرد نيته قوله : (الجنب لمس المصحف فقد الشرط الأوّل فيه وهو كونه عبادة . قوله : (أو دخول المسجد) فقد فيه العبادة، وإن كان لا يحل بغير طهارة من الأكبر. قوله : (أو) تعليم الغير) فقد فيه الثالث، وهو كونه لا يصح، ة، أو لا يحل بدون طهارة، وإن كان عبادة مقصودة كما قاله الشرح قوله : (وكذا لزيارة القبور) فقد فيها الثالث أيضاً قوله : ( والأذان) إنتفى فيه الثاني، والثالث وكذا الإقامة. قوله : (والسلام ورده إنتفى فيه الثالث فقط، وكذا الإسلام قوله : (وقال أبو حنيفة ومحمد : لا تصح لأنه إنما جعل التراب طهور للمسلم فقط بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «التراب طهور المسلم قوله : (فهو على الخلاف فعلى قولهما لا تصح به الصلاة لأنها ليست قربة مقصودة، وعلى قول محمد تصح لأنها قربة عنده قاله في البحر عن الترشيح قوله : (وفي رواية النوادر) المراد بالنوادر كتب غير ظاهر الرواية كما تقدّم التنبيه عليه في الخطبة لا أنها اسم كتاب . قوله : (بمجرد نيته) أي التيمم هو مقابل لما في المصنف ولا إعتماد على هذه الرواية، كما نبه على ذلك الكمال.
For (touching) the mus-haf, or entering the mosque, or teaching others: his prayer is not valid with it (tayammum) according to the most correct opinion, and similarly for visiting graves, and the adhan, and iqamah, and the greeting (salam) and its reply, or for embracing Islam according to the generality of the shaykhs. Abu Yusuf said: His prayer is valid with it because it enters into Islam, for it is the head of devotional acts. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said: It is not valid, and that is the most correct opinion. And if he performed tayammum for the prostration of gratitude (sajdat al-shukr), then it is subject to the difference (of opinion) as we will mention. And in the riwayah of Nawadir and al-Hasan: its permissibility by his mere intention. (Commentary:) [The commentator said:] The janub for touching the mus-haf loses the first condition in it (tayammum), which is that it be a devotional act. Or entering the mosque loses the devotional act (in tayammum), although it is not permissible without taharah from major impurity. Or teaching others loses the third condition, which is that it is not valid or not permissible without taharah, although it is an intended devotional act as stated in the Sharh. Similarly for visiting graves, it also loses the third condition. For the adhan, the second and third conditions are absent, and similarly for iqamah. For the greeting and its reply, only the third is lost. Similarly for Islam. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said: It is not valid because earth was made a purifier only for the Muslim, by his (saws) saying: 'Earth is a purifier for the Muslim.' He said: It is subject to difference: according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) on their view, prayer with it is not valid because it is not an intended devotional act; according to Muhammad it is valid because it is a devotional act in his view. This is stated in al-Bahr from al-Tarshih. He said: Regarding the riwayah of Nawadir, the intended meaning of Nawadir is the books other than Zahir al-Riwayah, as was pointed out in the khutbah, not that it is the name of a book. He said: By mere intention, meaning tayammum is opposite to what is in the matn, and there is no reliance on this riwayah, as al-Kamal pointed out.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of salah performed with tayammum that was done for a purpose other than salah itself. The text lists several acts: touching the mus-haf (Qur'an), entering the mosque, teaching others, visiting graves, giving adhan, iqamah, greeting (salam) and its reply, and embracing Islam. According to the majority of shaykhs, if one performs tayammum with the intention of doing any of these acts, then prays with that same tayammum, the prayer is invalid. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that the prayer is valid because tayammum is a means to enter into Islam, which is the greatest act of worship. However, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani maintain that the prayer is not valid, and this is the relied-upon opinion. The commentary explains that these acts lack one or more of the conditions required for tayammum to be a valid substitute for wudu in prayer. For example, touching the mus-haf is not itself an act of worship (the first condition), entering the mosque is an act of worship but does not require wudu (the third condition), etc. The commentary also clarifies that the narration from Nawadir (which are books outside the six core works of Zahir al-Riwayah) and al-Hasan allowing tayammum for sajdat al-shukr by mere intention is not relied upon.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution using clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
النوادر (al-nawadir): Books of rare transmissions outside the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, if someone performs tayammum with the intention of entering the mosque and then prays, what is the ruling on his prayer?
A) It is valid because tayammum is a purifier.
B) It is invalid because the tayammum was not done for a purpose that requires taharah for prayer.
C) It is valid if he recites Quran during the prayer.
D) It is invalid only if he is in the desert.

Key Takeaway
The validity of salah after tayammum depends on the intention behind the tayammum: it must be for a purpose that itself requires wudu or ghusl.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Distance as an Excuse for Tayammum: The Mile Standard
Condition of distance from water as an excuse permitting tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum due to distance from water and explain the measurement system used to define the mile.

Core Idea
Tayammum is permitted when water is a mile away — and the mile is defined by a precise chain of customary measurements.

In this lesson, we examine the condition of distance from water that permits tayammum. The Hanafi school defines this distance as a mile, using a detailed system of customary measurements. Understanding this system is essential for correctly applying the ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excuse and its condition
The text addresses the condition of being a certain distance from pure water. The excuse is distance, and the condition is that the distance be at least a mile.
2
Define the mile
Learn the traditional definition: 1 mile = 1000 paces (ba'), each pace = 4 cubits (dhira'), each cubit = 4 handspans, each handspan = 20 fingerbreadths, down to barleycorns and hairs. Also: 1 farsakh = 3 miles, 1 barid = 4 farsakhs.
3
Recognize the role of predominant opinion
The distance is estimated by ghalabat al-zann (predominant opinion), which has the force of certainty in fiqh rulings. This means you do not need exact measurement; strong probability suffices.
This is a key Hanafi principle.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The text states that the estimation by the mile is 'al-mukhtar' (the chosen) and 'al-mashhur' (well-known) among the majority of scholars.
5
Apply to tayammum
If you are a mile or more from water, or if you estimate by predominant opinion that water is that far, tayammum is permitted as a rukhsah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( كبعده أي الشخص ميلا ضبط بعضهم الميل والفرسخ، والبريد في قوله : إن الـبـريـد مـن الـفـراسـخ أربع ولفرسخ فثلاث أميال ضــعــوا والميل ألف أي من الباعات قل والباع أربع أذرع فــتــتــبــعــوا ثم الذراع من الأصابع أربع من بعدها العشرون، ثم الإصبع شعيرات فظهر شعيرة منها إلى بطن لأخـرى تــوضــع ثم الشعيرة ست شعرات فقط من ذيل بغل ليس عن ذا مرجع قاله في الفتح والميل في اللغة منتهى مد البصر . قوله : (بغلبة الظن فإن لها حكم اليقين في الفقهيات قوله هو المختار) أي التقدير بالميل هو المختار، وهو المشهور عند الجمهور. قوله: (وهي ذراع ونصف) فجملة ذرعانه ستة آلاف، وبعضهم ضبطه في القدم بنصف ساعة. قوله : (بذراع العامة هو المذكور في النظم. قوله : (عن ماء طهور) أي كاف.
[The commentator said:] (His distance) i.e., the person (by a mile). Some defined the mile, farsakh, and barid in verses: Indeed the barid is four farsakhs, and for the farsakh they set three miles, and the mile is a thousand, meaning of paces, and the pace (ba') is four cubits, so follow that. Then the cubit (dhira') is four handspans, after that twenty (fingerbreadths?), then the finger (isba') has barleycorns, then a barleycorn from its outer to the belly of another is placed, then the barleycorn is six hairs only from the tail of a mule, there is no return from this. He said this in al-Fath. And the mile in language is the limit of eyesight. He said: (By predominant opinion) for it has the ruling of certainty in fiqh matters. He said: (It is the chosen) i.e., the estimation by the mile is the chosen, and it is well-known among the majority. He said: (And it is a cubit and a half) so its total length is six thousand (units?), and some defined it by foot as half an hour. He said: (By the common cubit) is that mentioned in the poem. He said: (From pure water) i.e., sufficient.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage explains the second condition for the permissibility of tayammum: the excuse that permits it. One such excuse is being a mile away from water. The commentator defines the mile using traditional measurements: a mile is 1000 paces (ba'), each pace is 4 cubits (dhira'), each cubit is 4 handspans, each handspan is 20 fingerbreadths, and so on down to barleycorns and hairs. A farsakh is 3 miles, and a barid is 4 farsakhs. The estimation of distance is based on predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann), which in fiqh has the force of certainty. The relied-upon view is that the distance is measured by the mile, as this is the most well-known among the majority of scholars. The commentary also clarifies that the water must be pure (tahur) and sufficient for purification. Even if the person is within a town (misr), the ruling applies unless specific conditions prevent it, as mentioned in other parts of the hashya.

Key Terms
الميل (al-mil): A unit of distance defined as 1000 paces (ba'), each pace being 4 cubits (dhira'), approximately 1.5 modern miles? But here it is set as 1/3 farsakh and defined in detail.
غَلَبَةُ الظَّنِّ (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant opinion or strong probability, which in fiqh matters has the legal force of certainty (yaqin) for practical rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the measure of distance from water that permits tayammum according to the chosen Hanafi position?
A) One farsakh.
B) One mile (1/3 farsakh).
C) Two miles.
D) The distance a person can walk in one hour.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tayammum when water is a mile away, and this distance is estimated by predominant opinion, which holds the force of certainty in fiqh.
